  <div id="keyfeatures">

    <h2><strong>key features</strong></h2>

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">personas</p>
      <p>A persona is a community focused on a particular passion. Choose 5 out of 100+ personas you most identify with.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">folio</p>
      <p>Your folio is a personalized feed of content relevant to your chosen personas.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">potentials</p>
      <p>Potentials are people we'd like to introduce you to, based on your personas, location and personality.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">connections</p>
      <p>Create more meaningful connections with our direct messaging feature, including photos, gifts and unique expressions.</p>
    </div>  

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">leaderboards</p>
      <p>The more interactions your contributions generate, the more likely you will become a persona leader.</p>
    </div>

    <div class="threecol">
      <p class="title">milestones &amp; rewards</p>
      <p>Reach milestones, unlock rewards, and add layers of fun to your social connections as you venture through hello.</p>
    </div>

<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<figure colspan="2"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Adele_-_Hello_(Official_Single_Cover).png" class="image"><img alt="A dark black-and-white image of Adele holding a telephone to her ear" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Adele_-_Hello_%28Official_Single_Cover%29.png/220px-Adele_-_Hello_%28Official_Single_Cover%29.png" width="220" height="220"></a></figure>

								
												
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
<p>"<b>Hello</b>" is a song by English singer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adele" title="Adele">Adele</a>. It was released on 23 October 2015 by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/XL_Recordings" title="XL Recordings">XL Recordings</a> as the lead single from her third studio album, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/25_(Adele_album)" title="25 (Adele album)">25</a></i> (2015). Adele co-wrote the song with her producer, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Kurstin" title="Greg Kurstin">Greg Kurstin</a>. "Hello" is a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Piano_ballad" title="Piano ballad">piano ballad</a> with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> influences, and lyrics that discuss themes of nostalgia and regret. Upon release, the song was well received by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music_critics" class="mw-redirect" title="Music critics">music critics</a>, who compared it favourably to Adele's previous work and praised the song's lyrics and Adele's vocals.</p>
<p>"Hello" attained international commercial success reaching number one in almost every country it charted in, including the United Kingdom, where it became her second UK number-one single, following "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Someone_like_You_(Adele_song)" title="Someone like You (Adele song)">Someone like You</a>", and has the largest opening week sales in three years. In the United States, "Hello" debuted atop the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>, becoming Adele's fourth number-one on the chart and breaking several records, including becoming the first song to sell over a million digital copies in a week. By the end of 2015, it had sold 12.3 million units globally (combined sales and track-equivalent streams) and was the year's 7th best-selling single.<sup id="cite_ref-IFPI_2-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-IFPI-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The accompanying music video was directed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavier_Dolan" title="Xavier Dolan">Xavier Dolan</a> and co-stars Adele and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tristan_Wilds" title="Tristan Wilds">Tristan Wilds</a>. The music video for the song broke the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vevo_Record" class="mw-redirect" title="Vevo Record">Vevo Record</a> by achieving over 27.7 million views within a 24-hour span, held previously by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bad_Blood_(Taylor_Swift_song)" title="Bad Blood (Taylor Swift song)">Bad Blood</a>" which accumulated 20.1 million views in that timeframe. It also broke the record for shortest time to attain 100 million <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vevo" title="Vevo">Vevo</a> views, previously held by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>' "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrecking_Ball_(Miley_Cyrus_song)" title="Wrecking Ball (Miley Cyrus song)">Wrecking Ball</a>", as well as shortest time to reach 1 billion <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> views (88 days). Adele promoted the song with a live performance on a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a> one-hour-long special, entitled <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adele_at_the_BBC" title="Adele at the BBC">Adele at the BBC</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_and_composition">Writing and composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Writing and composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" width="50" height="50"></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist">
<div class="haudio">
<div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Adele_-_Hello_Clip.ogg" title="File:Adele - Hello Clip.ogg">"Hello" (2015)</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer"><audio id="mwe_player_0" class="kskin">
<source src="https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/f4/Adele_-_Hello_Clip.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source>
<track src="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:Adele_-_Hello_Clip.ogg.en.srt&amp;action=raw&amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt" type="text/x-srt" title="TimedText:Adele_-_Hello_Clip.ogg.en.srt" dir="ltr" label="English (en) subtitles"></track></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description">A 21-second sample of "Hello"'s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refrain" title="Refrain">chorus</a>, where Adele is singing the lines over layers of backing vocals, piano and drums "towards a very luscious wall of sound".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_3-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-telegraph-3">[3]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="mbox-text"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"Hello" was written by Adele and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Kurstin" title="Greg Kurstin">Greg Kurstin</a> and produced by the latter. Kurstin also played bass, guitar, drums, piano and keyboards, while Adele also played drums.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> "Hello" was written in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chiswick" title="Chiswick">Chiswick</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, something not normally done by Adele, who said she likes to write her music at home.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> The writing process for the song was slow, taking six months to complete. Initially Adele and Kurstin started writing the first verse; finishing half of the song, six months later Adele contacted Kurstin to finish the song with her, with Kurstin stating he was not sure "if Adele was ever going to come back and finish it."<sup id="cite_ref-RTm_6-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-RTm-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Hello" is a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Soul_music" title="Soul music">soul</a> piano ballad,<sup id="cite_ref-SGum_1-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-SGum-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> played in the key of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/F_minor" title="F minor">F minor</a> at a tempo of 79 beats per minute. The repeated chord progression heard in the verse, played by the piano, follows a progression of Fm–A<span class="music-symbol">♭</span>–E<span class="music-symbol">♭</span>–D<span class="music-symbol">♭</span>. According to Musicnotes.com, Adele's vocals span from F<sub>3</sub> to A<span class="music-symbol">♭</span><sub>5</sub> in the song.<sup id="cite_ref-Vocalrange_8-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-Vocalrange-8">[8]</a></sup> During the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chorus_(song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chorus (song)">chorus</a> Adele is heard singing the lines over layers of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backing_vocals" class="mw-redirect" title="Backing vocals">backing vocals</a>, piano and drums which were described by the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> as leaning "towards a very luscious wall of sound".<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-telegraph-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>Lyrically, the song focuses on themes of nostalgia and regret and plays out like a conversation. The song was noted for containing themes of regret and was seen as a follow-up to her single "Someone like You" appearing to reflect on a failed relationship. The song's lyrics were also seen as being conversational, revolving around "all the relationships of her past", ranging from friends, family members and ex-partners.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Speaking on the song's lyrical content, Adele told <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Grimshaw" title="Nick Grimshaw">Nick Grimshaw</a> on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> Breakfast Show: "I felt all of us were moving on, and it's not about an ex-relationship, a love relationship, it's about my relationship with everyone that I love. It's not that we have fallen out, we've all got our lives going on and I needed to write that song so they would all hear it, because I'm not in touch with them."<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> According to Adele, the line "Hello from the other side" signifies "the other side of becoming an adult, making it out alive from your late teens, early twenties."<sup id="cite_ref-RTm_6-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-RTm-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_reception">Release and reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Release and reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On 18 October 2015, a 30-second clip of "Hello" was played during a commercial break on <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_TV_series)" title="The X Factor (UK TV series)">The X Factor</a></i> in the United Kingdom. The commercial teased what was then new material, with her vocals accompanied by lyrics on a black screen.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Josh Duboff of <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)" title="Vanity Fair (magazine)">Vanity Fair</a></i> wrote that "the Internet collectively lost its mind" after the broadcast of the trailer.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> On 22 October, Adele announced the upcoming release of <i>25</i> to her fans on Twitter. She also shared that "Hello" would be released on 23 October as the lead single off of the album.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CoS_14-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-CoS-14">[14]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AXS_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-AXS-15">[15]</a></sup> On 23 October, Adele joined <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nick_Grimshaw" title="Nick Grimshaw">Nick Grimshaw</a>'s show on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> for the song's premiere.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexis_Petridis" title="Alexis Petridis">Alexis Petridis</a> of <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i> described it as "a big ballad, but a superior example of its kind", and opined that the song is "precisely the kind of lovelorn epic ballad that made Adele one of the biggest stars in the world."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Writing for <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i>, Emily Jupp stated in her review of the song that it "might not be groundbreaking, but Adele's return with her familiar, smoky sound is very welcome". She called it an <span>"</span>'if it ain't broke' ballad" and said: "Adele does what she does best, belting out emotional tales of love and loss much the same as with her last album, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/21_(Adele_album)" title="21 (Adele album)">21</a></i>, but this time, with a little more self-forgiveness."<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greg_Kot" title="Greg Kot">Greg Kot</a> of the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i> wrote: "Lyrics that work best when they zoom in on personal details match her combination of vocal power and restraint."<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> Neil McCormick from <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> called it "a beautiful song of loss and regret", adding that "it takes a grip on the kind of memory every listener holds somewhere in their heart and merges it with Adele's own drama."<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_3-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-telegraph-3">[3]</a></sup> <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> ranked "Hello" at number 6 on its year-end list to find the 50 best songs of 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> Several publications have commented on similarities in the theme of the song and accompanying video with that of "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Lionel_Richie_song)" title="Hello (Lionel Richie song)">Hello</a>" by American singer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lionel_Richie" title="Lionel Richie">Lionel Richie</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Horton_22-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-Horton-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_and_Oceania">Europe and Oceania</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Europe and Oceania">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Three days after its release, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_Charts_Company" title="Official Charts Company">Official Charts Company</a> announced that "Hello" had accumulated 165,000 chart sales in the United Kingdom, of which 156,000 were downloads.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> "Hello" entered at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a> on 30 October 2015, –  for the week dated 5 November 2015 –  with 333,000 combined sales, of which 259,000 were downloads, making it the biggest selling number-one single on the chart in three years. It marked Adele's second UK number-one single, after 2011's "Someone like You". Additionally, "Hello" was streamed 7.32 million times in its first week, breaking the streaming record previously held by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/What_Do_You_Mean%3F" title="What Do You Mean?">What Do You Mean?</a>". Including streaming sales and excluding <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" class="mw-redirect" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i> and <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pop_Idol" title="Pop Idol">Pop Idol</a></i> winners' singles, major charity campaign records and Christmas number ones, "Hello" was the second biggest selling number one of the 21st century in the UK, beaten only by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shaggy_(musician)" title="Shaggy (musician)">Shaggy</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/It_Wasn%27t_Me" title="It Wasn't Me">It Wasn't Me</a>", which sold 345,000 copies in a week in February 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-UK_number_1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-UK_number_1-25">[25]</a></sup> The following week the song remained at number one on the UK Singles Charts, "Hello" sold a further 121,000 downloads and was streamed 5.78 million times, the same week the song was certified Gold by the BPI.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_26-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-auto-26">[26]</a></sup> On Friday 20 May 2016 it spent it's 30th week in the UK Top 100. The song also debuted at number one in Belgium, Czech Republic, France, Germany, Greece, Hungary, Ireland, Israel, Italy, Lebanon, Luxembourg, The Netherlands, Norway, Portugal, Scotland, Slovakia, Spain and Switzerland.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In Australia, "Hello" entered at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ARIA_Charts" title="ARIA Charts">ARIA Singles Chart</a> on 31 October 2015, selling over 59,075 units, which earned the song a gold certification in its first week. The song also became the second fastest-selling single of the year, behind <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/See_You_Again_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="See You Again (Wiz Khalifa song)">See You Again</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-maricrisfaderugao_28-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-maricrisfaderugao-28">[28]</a></sup> It marked Adele's second number-one single on the ARIA Singles Chart following 2011's "Someone like You".<sup id="cite_ref-AUS_number_1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-AUS_number_1-29">[29]</a></sup> The single stayed atop the chart for a second week and was certified platinum selling over 70,000 units.<sup id="cite_ref-maricrisfaderugao_28-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-maricrisfaderugao-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>In New Zealand, the song debuted at number one on the New Zealand singles chart, holding the position the following week and was certified platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="North_America">North America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: North America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the United States, "Hello" debuted at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> on 2 November 2015, for the chart dated 14 November 2015, becoming only the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Billboard_Hot_100_chart_achievements_and_milestones#Number-one_debuts" title="List of Billboard Hot 100 chart achievements and milestones">24th song to debut at number one</a>. "Hello" started at number 49 on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_Songs" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio Songs">Radio Songs</a> chart, after three days of release. In its first full week of airplay, it rose from 45 to 9, up 146% to 70 million all format audience impressions. The track started at number one on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/On-Demand_Songs" title="On-Demand Songs">On-Demand Songs</a> chart with a record 20.4 million on-demand streams, becoming her first number-one song on the chart. "Hello" entered at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Digital_Songs" title="Digital Songs">Digital Songs</a> chart with sales of 1,112,000, becoming the first track to sell over one million digital copies in a single week and almost doubling the record for the most downloads sold in a week, previously held by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flo_Rida" title="Flo Rida">Flo Rida</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Right_Round" title="Right Round">Right Round</a>", which sold 636,000 downloads in the week ending 28 February 2009. "Hello" started with 61.6 million US streams, becoming her first number-one song and the second greatest weekly total on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Streaming_Songs" title="Streaming Songs">Streaming Songs</a> chart, behind <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Baauer" title="Baauer">Baauer</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Harlem_Shake_(song)" title="Harlem Shake (song)">Harlem Shake</a>", which registered 103 million streams on week of 3 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-US_number_1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-US_number_1-31">[31]</a></sup> "Hello" is the first song to sell more than a million digital copies in a single week and the third highest weekly sales total since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> began tracking sales in 1991. Only <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elton_John" title="Elton John">Elton John</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Candle_in_the_Wind_1997" title="Candle in the Wind 1997">Candle in the Wind 1997/Something About the Way You Look Tonight</a>" has sold more in a single week, selling 3.446 million copies in its opening week and 1.212 million copies in its second week.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>In its second week, "Hello" stayed at number one on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, selling another 635,000 digital copies marking the third-best digital sales week and the highest for a non-debut week. "Hello" also held atop Streaming Songs with 47.4 million US streams, down 23 percent from 61.6 million in its first week, the track also stayed atop the On-Demand Songs with 18.1 million streams. On the Radio Songs chart, "Hello" moved from 9 to 6, up by 46% to 106 million all-format audience impressions, thus becoming the top Airplay Gainer on the Hot 100. The track also moved from two to one on the Adult Alternative Songs airplay chart and moved nine to four on the Adult Contemporary format.<sup id="cite_ref-auto1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-auto1-33">[33]</a></sup> The following week, the song stayed at the top of the Hot 100 and Digital Songs chart, selling 480,000 downloads and becoming just the third song to sell over 400,000 copies for three straight weeks. "Hello" also rose from 6 to 1 on the Radio Songs chart in just its fourth week (the greatest leap to number one on the chart's 25-year history), marking the quickest climb to number one on the chart in 22 years, since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dreamlover_(Mariah_Carey_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dreamlover (Mariah Carey song)">Dreamlover</a>" reached the top in its fourth frame on 28 August 1993. Additionally, "Hello" became just the third song to top the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hot_100" class="mw-redirect" title="Hot 100">Hot 100</a>, Digital Songs, Streaming Songs, On-Demand Songs and Radio Songs tallies simultaneously in the nearly three years all five charts had coexisted. "Hello" remained atop the Hot 100 for ten consecutive weeks, becoming only the 31st No. 1 in the Hot 100's history to reign for at least 10 weeks. By spending a tenth week at the top of the chart, it became Adele's longest-running number-one single and the longest-leading Hot 100 No. 1 since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wiz_Khalifa" title="Wiz Khalifa">Wiz Khalifa</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/See_You_Again_(Wiz_Khalifa_song)" title="See You Again (Wiz Khalifa song)">See You Again</a>," featuring <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlie_Puth" title="Charlie Puth">Charlie Puth</a>, which ruled for 12 weeks in 2015. "Hello" also logged the most weeks atop the Hot 100 by a solo female since <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/We_Found_Love" title="We Found Love">We Found Love</a>," featuring <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calvin_Harris" title="Calvin Harris">Calvin Harris</a>, which led for 10 weeks in 2011–2012. As of January 2016, it had sold 3.7 million downloads.<sup id="cite_ref-ussales_34-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-ussales-34">[34]</a></sup> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> certified the song quadruple platinum.<sup id="cite_ref-riaa_35-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-riaa-35">[35]</a></sup> The single also benefitted from numerous Dance/EDM remixes as well,<sup id="cite_ref-AdeleRemixes_36-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-AdeleRemixes-36">[36]</a></sup> thus resulting in "Hello" topping <i>Billboard's</i> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance_Club_Songs" title="Dance Club Songs">Dance Club Songs</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dance/Mix_Show_Airplay" title="Dance/Mix Show Airplay">Dance/Mix Show Airplay</a> charts.<sup id="cite_ref-AdeleDanceCharts_37-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-AdeleDanceCharts-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AdeleDanceNumberOne_38-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-AdeleDanceNumberOne-38">[38]</a></sup> On the chart dated 23 April 2016, the song spent a 21st week at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adult_Contemporary_Chart" class="mw-redirect" title="Adult Contemporary Chart">Adult Contemporary Chart</a>, matching the record set by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kelly_Clarkson" title="Kelly Clarkson">Kelly Clarkson</a>'s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Breakaway_(Kelly_Clarkson_song)" title="Breakaway (Kelly Clarkson song)">Breakaway</a> (2005) and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a>'s <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A_New_Day_Has_Come_(song)" title="A New Day Has Come (song)">A New Day Has Come</a> (2002) for the longest No. 1 run among women since the list launched in 1961. It also equaled the third-longest stay at the summit among all acts.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Hello" entered at the top of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_Hot_100" title="Canadian Hot 100">Canadian Hot 100</a> as the 100th song to top the chart, selling 140,000 copies and outsold <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Justin_Bieber" title="Justin Bieber">Justin Bieber</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sorry_(Justin_Bieber_song)" title="Sorry (Justin Bieber song)">Sorry</a>", which sold 40,000 units and debuted at number two the same week. The song was streamed 4.79 million times, setting a record for the most streamed track in a week.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_video">Music video</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Music video">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox">
<div class="">
<div>
<p>"When I heard the song I saw a story right away. [The video] is highly unoriginal. The lyrics are 'Hello, it's me' and then you see someone picking up a phone. I'm not good at imagining super conceptual videos. I just thought it would be nice to have her walk around the house and make phone calls and end up in a forest, with maybe some flashbacks in it."</p>
<p>—Dolan, behind the concept of the music video<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_41-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-LATimes-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The accompanying music video for the song was directed by Canadian actor and director <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Xavier_Dolan" title="Xavier Dolan">Xavier Dolan</a> and released on 22 October 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> The concept of the video revolves around a recently broken-up woman calling a younger version of herself.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_41-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-LATimes-41">[41]</a></sup> Portions of the video—mostly the finale on the pond and the shot of her opening her eyes in the beginning—were filmed with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cameras, making it the first music video in IMAX format.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The video draws inspiration from Dolan's semi-autobiographical debut <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/I_Killed_My_Mother" title="I Killed My Mother">I Killed My Mother</a></i>, which was made when Dolan was barely 20.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_41-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-LATimes-41">[41]</a></sup> The video was filmed on a farm in Québec over 4 days in September 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-LATimes_41-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-LATimes-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The video stars American actor <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tristan_Wilds" title="Tristan Wilds">Tristan Wilds</a>. Dolan contacted Wilds via Skype and explained the concept for the video, which Wilds agreed to take part in.<sup id="cite_ref-ew.com_45-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-ew.com-45">[45]</a></sup> During the filming both Adele and Wilds were asked to improvise and "tap into" their past relationships in order to convey the correct emotions. Dolan also filmed shots of both Adele and Wilds having conversations and laughing.<sup id="cite_ref-ew.com_45-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-ew.com-45">[45]</a></sup> The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sepia_tone" class="mw-redirect" title="Sepia tone">sepia toned</a> video shows Adele performing the song in a small house and outside in a wooded forest, intercut with scenes of her making a tearful phone call and flashbacks to a past relationship with Wilds' character.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flip_phone" class="mw-redirect" title="Flip phone">flip phone</a> used by Adele in the video was widely commented upon due to being of a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Retro_style" title="Retro style">retro style</a>. Dolan replied to the remarks by saying: "It makes me uncomfortable filming iPhones because I feel like I'm shooting a commercial. Those things: iPhones, laptops, all those elements, to me, they bring me back to reality: That's not what you want. You want to get out of your own life; you want to enter someone else's; you want to travel somewhere; you want to be told a story. I'm realizing maybe I've been more distracting than anything else with that flip phone, but it wasn't intentional!"<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The music video for the song broke the previous <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vevo_Record" class="mw-redirect" title="Vevo Record">Vevo Record</a> by achieving over 27.7 million views within a 24-hour period.<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian-Groves_48-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-Guardian-Groves-48">[48]</a></sup> Later, the video continued to break <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Miley_Cyrus" title="Miley Cyrus">Miley Cyrus</a>'s "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wrecking_Ball_(Miley_Cyrus_song)" title="Wrecking Ball (Miley Cyrus song)">Wrecking Ball</a>" Vevo record for the fastest video to reach 100 million views in 5 days.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The phrase "Adele hello" was also the top YouTube search term of Friday and Saturday, and on average the video was getting one million views per hour during the first two days, peaking at 1.6 million in a single hour, beating the peak view rate of the trailer for <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i>, which peaked at 1.2 million views per hour.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of 19 June 2016, the video has become the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_most_viewed_YouTube_videos" title="List of most viewed YouTube videos">5th most viewed video</a> on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> having earned over 1.59 billion views.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>The video also became the third video on YouTube to reach 10 million likes on May 29, 2016. The only other two videos to have over 10 million likes are "Gangnam Style" and "See You Again".</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Adele performed "Hello" live for the first time for a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC one-hour-long special</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adele_at_the_BBC" title="Adele at the BBC">Adele at the BBC</a></i>, which was recorded on 2 November and was broadcast on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/BBC_One" title="BBC One">BBC One</a> on 20 November.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> She also performed the song at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NRJ_Music_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="NRJ Music Awards">17th NRJ Music Awards</a> on 7 November 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Radio_City_Music_Hall" title="Radio City Music Hall">Radio City Music Hall</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York" title="New York">New York</a> on 17 November 2015 as her opening number (<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adele_Live_in_New_York_City" title="Adele Live in New York City">Adele Live in New York City</a></i>), and on <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on 21 November 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> On 23 November 2015, after appearing on <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Tonight_Show_Starring_Jimmy_Fallon" title="The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon">The Tonight Show Starring Jimmy Fallon</a></i>, Adele recorded the song with Fallon and his house band, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Roots" title="The Roots">The Roots</a></i>, playing classroom instruments. The version was broadcast on the show the following night.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> On 13 December 2015 Adele performed "Hello" on the <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/X_Factor" class="mw-redirect" title="X Factor">X Factor</a></i> live final at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wembley_Arena" title="Wembley Arena">The SSE Arena, Wembley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cover_versions">Cover versions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hello_(Adele_song)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Cover versions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>On November 9, 2015, British singer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rita_Ora" title="Rita Ora">Rita Ora</a> delivered her own version of the song by singing it in a self-invented language in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_(radio_network)" title="Capital (radio network)">Capital FM</a> studios.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></li>
<li>American singer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Demi_Lovato" title="Demi Lovato">Demi Lovato</a> covered "Hello" at the 2015 <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/KBKS-FM" title="KBKS-FM">106.1 KISS FM</a> Fall Ball in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">Seattle</a> on November 14, 2015. Her rendition of the song was met with high critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> It eventually received a nomination for "Best Cover Song" at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3rd_iHeartRadio_Music_Awards" title="3rd iHeartRadio Music Awards">3rd iHeartRadio Music Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-nominees_63-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-nominees-63">[63]</a></sup> A fan video of Lovato's cover version has since garnered over 12.5 million views on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></li>
<li>During New Year's Eve 2016, Canadian singer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celine_Dion" title="Celine Dion">Celine Dion</a> put her own spin on "Hello" at her <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Celine_(residency_show)" title="Celine (residency show)">residency show</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></li>
<li>In December 2015, Washington, D.C.-based <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go-go" title="Go-go">go-go</a> band Backyard Band released a cover version of the song, which has since become widely popular in the area since its release.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hello_(Adele_song)#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
